< Text>
A few weeks ago I placed an online order on a Saturday. An hour had gone by. I called Domino's and they said their was no order in there system. I filed a complaint. Domino's corporate couldn't do anything since it was locally owned. They did reach out to them. about 10 days later this Domino's contacted me. I wasn't able to answer the phone but a message was left. I got sent a coupon for a free large 2 topping pizza. I thought this was fair.

About another week and a half went by. It was Friday about 8:18 pm. I thought it was pizza time, but I wasn't going to use the coupon because I wanted something else. So again I went online. Placed an order, but didn't pay for it online. I planned to walk there. I live 5 mins. from there so I figured I would just use my debit card when I got there. I grabbed my debit and took a walk. I arrived, I said I'm here for my order, I handed over my debit card, and I was asked for ID. I don't know if this is a new thing but it isn't common to ask for ID when using your debit. I said I don't have my ID. I just grabbed it and walked here. He said I need an ID. Already frustrated I turned to my girlfriend to see if she had cash. She did not. Again we didn't think this was going to happen. So we began to walk out when the guy said, did you still want the pizza? I said, no I'm not going to walk home and walk back.

We ended up going to Papa John's. I place I've never bought pizza from. They just got a new customer. The Meats pizza was loaded with meat! Domino's equivalent is not as meaty!

Domino's was in the distant past at this time...so I thought. At about 10:49 pm I got a phone call from Domino's. They left me a VM. It said, we will be closing shortly (they close at 1 am on Friday, not what I call shortly). They said your pizza is ready for pick up. Why the hell are you calling me 2.5 hours after the order was placed and that late?

FYI, I won't be using that free pizza coupon. Done with this location. This was the same Domino's I used to ride my bike to as a kid every Friday for pizza night. I don't know what happened here. Sometimes when your dealing with people you need to adjust to the circumstances. Understand that not everybody is trying to scam. I should of heard something like, OK sir, don't worry about, next just bring your ID, they got us doing that now, thanks for coming, etc. That didn't happen today.<//Text>

<date>1622179586953< /date><Rate>5< /Rate><text>Quaint Italian restaurant on Balboa Island's main drag (Marine Ave).  Old world decor.  Excellent and very attentive service by an older gentleman, who I presumed to be the owner.  Prices are very reasonable given the quality of the food, size of the servings, and the location.

The warm lightly toasted Italian bread was perfect, especially when dipped in olive oil and balsamic vinegar, and also when slathered with the whipped butter.

My wife had a seafood risotto, which was very much like cioppino over risotto.  Very tasty.  Her green salad was also quite nice, with crisp mixed greens and tomatoes, and a nice, light vinaigrette dressing.

I began with the warm chorizo appetizer.  This actually turned out to be almost a meal in itself.  An entr√©e-sized plate of thickly sliced chorizo and grilled bell peppers and finely minced tomatoes, all lovingly embraced by a light tomato-based sauce, this savory appetizer went down with ease, leaving me somewhat full, already.

My caesar salad was also excellent, with crisp dark green romaine leaves and a zesty caesar dressing that lightly coated the romaine leaves (just the way I like it).

For my main dish, I had the lobster ravioli, swimming in a creamy tomato-based cardinale sauce.  The soft little pasta pillows were packed with lobster and cheese, and were very yummy.

This was our first visit, and we plan to return soon.< /text>< pictures>

< review>
My goodness, where do I start?

I called 5 minutes prior asking if there was availability for two on Valentine's. The gentleman on the phone said "yes, come on down!" Walked in a little after 7 p.m. The lady addressed us and immediately asked if we had reservations, I replied "no, but I just called". This is a small restaurant of 11 tables, 7 inside with 4 on the front patio.  There were 5 empty tables when we arrived, 2 inside and 3 outside. She said that we could only sit outside. Throughout our dining, there continued to be turn over and empty tables available inside. Meanwhile, my elderly Mother with stage 4 cancer and I remain outside... OK fine. Strike 1.

Because we were sitting outside, my Mom ordered hot water to stay warm, the same lady (I assume the owner operating with her husband and the only food servers), replies with, "the kitchen is crazy, and there is no room to boil water"...hmmmm OK. Strike 2

Ordered the calamari for an appetizer, and it came out within reasonable time. It wasn't greasy, and the tomato sauce which accompanied it was good, but overly salted. The portion was very small and so were the rings of calamari...a bit shocking actually...
more like little morsels . Strike 3

Also ordered the Veal Saltimbocca which is one of my favorite Italian dishes. $31!!!!! First, it took more than 20 minutes to arrive, and the restaurant was half empty. The plate was laid 3/4's on our table with the edge hanging off. The veal was so thin and tough, therefore it shouldn't have taken that long to make.  It was so salty, way too lemony, and hardly any flavor of sage. The prosciutto overpowered the little pieces of veal...it was all wrong. Strike 4

I also ordered a glass of Chianti, which never showed, but appeared on my bill. When I pointed it out, the lady responded with, "dear, you could have told me". Sorry, that is not my job. Strike 5

In addition, our glasses of water were not once refilled, nor did anyone ask how our dinner was.

Unfortunately, I can't give zero üåü s. Not sure how this place has decent ratings and are still in business. I get they are a small restaurant in a touristy location, but maybe that's how they make it, by ripping off tourists who will never go back... like us. If you are charging those prices, there should be a certain level of service and quality. Sad.</review>

< text>
My date and I went after 8 and the owner served us, as the "OPEN" sign was lit, even though he told us he usually closes at 8 because it is dead on the island.
The food was marvelous; the chicken tender and the noodles perfect. My date had a Caesar salad, which had the perfect mix of vegetables and dressing, and I paired the chicken dish with a reasonably priced Italian Pinot Grigio.
I worked in various Italian restaurants and only go to Italian rarely anymore, because I am almost always disappointed, but this place will be where I go when I want Italian.<//text>

<Review>This is a lovely place to enjoy afternoon tea. Once greeted, we were seated inside the quaint house-remodeled restaurant and brought a tray of teas to smell. After selecting our choices (grapefruit oolong and honeybush apricot), our smile-prone waittress brought us cups of soup, momentarily followed by our tea and timely succeeded by a salad topped with fresh fruit. The tea was delicious and the food was a fine counterpart. After a cup's time, our triple-decker snack spread was delivered (see photo) and looked mouthwatering. Our waitress gave us a run down of the culinary selections. The scones were amazing, desserts delectable, and finger sandwiches, surprisingly filling. All an all a marvelous experience with wonderful flavors well worth the $25 per head price. Will be returning.

On the parking note: there is street parking, metered and unmetered (street sweeping Mon 10am-12pm) and there is also a public lot at the corner of the street past High Tea Cottage on the left that $2.50 for the day.</Review>< Time>

$60 a head for a three course, small portion, meal that specializes in an ambience made to exploit British enthusiasts rather than tea drinkers. No substitutions, though they will accommodate dietary restrictions. The teas are mostly herbal, very sweet, and limited to a selection of twenty or so. All teas are brewed with the same temperature and thrown in a pot, so expect a tanen heavy experience that becomes more bitter as you drink. All in all this place is good for a special occasion after lunch for people who want to feel like sophisticated tea drinkers, but don't actually drink a lot of tea.<//text>

< Text>
Everything was absolutely stellar, and my friend and I had a lovely time and left very full. Frankly, I was a bit trepidatious because of some of the poor reviews, but I can only guess that these must have been written by patrons who were not familiar with the experience of High Tea. Of course the management's insistence on both reservations and timeliness are necessary in a such a very small venue. The place is simply too small to accommodate drop-ins without a reservation. The owner was warm and gracious, the staff was attentive, and the food was well prepared, traditional high tea fair. If you are expecting huge deli sandwiches, High Tea is not for you. Scones with jam & clotted cream, and petite crust-less finger sandwiches are to be expected. If you have a larger appetite, additional soups and salads can be added for a fee. But if you want to stuff yourself... go to a burger place instead. You are paying for a relaxed and elegant experience...the same way you pay a lot more for coffee at Starbucks than at 7-11. I saw no evidence of any discriminatory behavior, as complained about by another reviewer. A group of very young girls sat next to us - white, Latina & African American - and the owner patiently answered all of their many questions about how it worked, prices for each item, etc. even though the teens clearly were not intending to spend much money, and were completely clueless about the ritual of Tea. My friend and I had a lovely experience and I am looking forward to returning with my elderly Mom soon!</Text>

<text>I had received the recall notice from Lexus, about the airbag situation with Takata.

I had only bought my used 2011 ES 350, a car I truly loved. Best I had ever owned... on 7/20/16. It was less than a year, I had owned it. My options given to me by corporate,  we're a rental (far cheaper quality) for minimum 6 months, or no one can ride in my passenger seat, until a fix is available. Maybe January of next year.

I went to my Lexus dealer, I bought the car from. I had a wonderful experience the first time. The Service Manager dealt with me personally, he brought the Sales Manager into it. Between them, they offered to make it right, if I wanted to trade the car in. A car, none of us could really do anything with.

That's when Rocky Tayeh, an Assistant Sales Manager entered the picture. He was asked if he could help me pick out something special, and they would try to make things right.

Rocky and I talked for a few minutes, while we walked to the cars. By the time we reached the lot, he knew which car he thought I might like. We end up at the same color, 2015 ES 350, updated model of my car. Obviously, very updated since 2011.

I looked at the price and Rocky noticed me cringe a bit. It was a L-Certified loaner car. Listed at a premium price. Rocky said, not to worry about that, they were gong to take care of me.

We went inside to talk a deal. I asked for a few concessions, he went to talk to the Sales Manager and they came back, with a deal... better than I asked for. They not only gave me full trade-in value for my old car, which they have to sit on, at least 6 months. They even added some to its value. They offered me the car at a price attractively below, what it was listed for. They offered me a finance rate, lower than I could get, if I borrowed the money from myself , through the credit union.

Just a very nice deal, on a great car... with zero haggling! Every question I had, Rocky had an answer, or he got one. He hooked me up with the Finance Manager, who had all the details, and we breezed through the paperwork. He was very clear, and I understood, everything... no behind the back, hidden fees. Heck, they took care of some of the fees I would normally have had to pay.

I saved thousands of dollars on a very nice Lexus. Thanks in large part to Rocky Tayeh. He's easy going, very respectful, and listens to people. I would most certainly buy a car from him again.
